<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_415315545">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/415315545" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh" class="left imgcol" title="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1346034704p2/10856439.jpg" alt="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/415315545?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 31, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh" class="user" title="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh">Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Paperback 9780060557812" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">subway commuters - Neil Gaiman and Urban Fantasy fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Florence (Lefty) by: </span>
      Ulrike Conrad
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=dark" class="actionLinkLite">dark</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=indulge" class="actionLinkLite">indulge</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=lit-brits" class="actionLinkLite">lit-brits</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=debut" class="actionLinkLite">debut</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=2013" class="actionLinkLite">2013</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=classics-modern" class="actionLinkLite">classics-modern</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer415315545">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18347146443646341278">Pure indulgence, the sort of book to tuck in with on a cold wet weekend. Again I'm trying out a new genre - for my 1st shot at ‘urban fantasy’ I picked this one, it's Gaiman’s solo debut. A premise that hooked because it made perfect sense to me. I mean anyone who’s taken a subway alone late at night, who’s glanced nervously down the track into a damp tunnel dimly lit by flickering lights would agree - if there IS a one-way portal to a subterranean world that’s where it's most likely to be...Plu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18347146443646341278">Pure indulgence, the sort of book to tuck in with on a cold wet weekend. Again I'm trying out a new genre - for my 1st shot at ‘urban fantasy’ I picked this one, it's Gaiman’s solo debut. A premise that hooked because it made perfect sense to me. I mean anyone who’s taken a subway alone late at night, who’s glanced nervously down the track into a damp tunnel dimly lit by flickering lights would agree - if there IS a one-way portal to a subterranean world that’s where it's most likely to be...Plus I’ve always loved subways, as a kid in Toronto I’d ride around aimlessly for hours just killing time, never outgrew it – done the same on 'grown-up' trips to New York &amp; London, and this story plays out in my favorite one of them all - London’s infamous Tube. <br /><em>“Understand this: there are two Londons. There’s London Above—that’s where you lived—and then there’s London Below—the Underside—inhabited by the people who fell through the cracks in the world. Now you’re one of them” </em><br />An adult fairytale with the prerequisite quest - not saying any more at risk of spoiling. Peopled with a host of weird &amp; wonderful characters like the Sewer Folk <em>"After the Great Stink they really came into their own, living in a world of gurgles and drips"</em>, the Rat-Speakers, a Marquis by the name of de Carabas that’s pretty special, a kick-ass warrior babe, there's even an angel. <br />Outshining them all though are Mr. Croup &amp; Mr Vandermar, the most delightfully wicked team of villains I’ve ever had the pleasure of coming across – <strong>worth reading just to make their acquaintance.</strong> In a voice like rancid butter it’s Mr. Croup who does most of the talking. <em>"I’m afraid we don’t have any redeeming features" </em>, who answers the phone <em>"Croup and Vandemar - eyes gouged, noses twisted, tongues pierced, chins cleft, throats slit."</em> When Mr. Vandemar does speak it's in a voice like a night wind blowing over a desert of bones. <em>"I’ll make you suffer, spoil your day."</em> Gross alert <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ Mr. Vandermar bites the heads off rats – this sort of behavior is so in character it didn’t really bother me - but fair warning  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Entertaining and just plain fun – a solid 4 stars.<br />_______________________________________<br /><strong>Cons:</strong> The 2 main characters are pretty weak. Richard Mayhew is an annoying wuss, though I liked him anyway &amp; Lady Door could definitely use some work... <br />Ramblings - not a spoiler: <strong>So what’s so SPECIAL about Gaiman?? </strong> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[My third this year I decided it was time I figured out why I keep going back for more, maybe in the process encourage you to give him a try. Truth is there are a TON of better writers – brighter, wittier, definitely more profound:) We all know authors who can out-write him, masters of the adventure, comedy, horror, suspense or fantasy novel. I'd say Gaiman’s brilliance is in his versatility, his ability to write competently in so many styles, to blend them into a well balanced mix that's uniquely his own. While his writing is simplistic and his characters admittedly lacking in depth he’s no slouch. Incredibly imaginative and wonderful at world building. Not great at 'suspending belief' I also appreciate his judicial restraint in the magic department - So if you're looking for escapist entertainment I'd say give him a try. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18347146443646341278">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_18527556">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18527556" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days" class="left imgcol" title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1420332941p2/395599.jpg" alt="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/18527556?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 29, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days" class="user" title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)">Shannon (Giraffe Days)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/474072.Neverwhere" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380789016" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=urban-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=2008" class="actionLinkLite">2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer18527556">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15154327847341970447">Richard Mayhew is an ordinary young man working in London, with a fiancee, Jessica, a small flat and a life more-or-less figured out. By Jessica. He's not a particularly brave man, or imaginative, and Jessica has his life all sorted for him. <br /><br />Everything in his life is turned upside-down - quite literally - when he stumbles across an injured girl on the footpath who asks for his help. Despite Jessica's insistence that he leave her there for someone else to take care of, he carries her back to his</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15154327847341970447">Richard Mayhew is an ordinary young man working in London, with a fiancee, Jessica, a small flat and a life more-or-less figured out. By Jessica. He's not a particularly brave man, or imaginative, and Jessica has his life all sorted for him. <br /><br />Everything in his life is turned upside-down - quite literally - when he stumbles across an injured girl on the footpath who asks for his help. Despite Jessica's insistence that he leave her there for someone else to take care of, he carries her back to his flat and at her behest, goes in search of someone called the Marquis de Carabas.<br /><br />By involving himself in her life, her world, he becomes invisible in his own. After the girl, Door, has gone back to London Below, Richard finds that no one can see him or hear him, that they've removed his desk at work and are renting out his apartment while he's in the bath. Jessica can't remember his name. The only thing left for him to do is seek out Door in London Below and somehow get his life back.<br /><br />The world of London Below is vivid, labrynthine, confusing, other-worldly, bizarre and smelly. The sewers, the Underground (the Tube) and a vast plane of tunnels, caverns and bunkers form curious homes for curious creatures, most of which Richard has trouble believing are real. To say he's a bit slow would be an understatement.<br /><br />He gets caught up in her mission to find out why her family was murdered and who wants her dead. Door has a unique talent - she can open any door, can create doors where they weren't before, and someone wants this skill badly enough to send two violent things after her, called Mister Croup and Mister Vandemar. She enlists the aid of a bodyguard, the famous Hunter, and goes on a quest to find the Angel Islington.<br /><br />--------------------------------------<br />I can't quite decide if I liked this book, really liked it, or thought it was just ok. It is fast-paced and peopled with numerous eccentric characters, and I did enjoy the book. It won't be a favourite of mine, though. I think, at the end of the day, I really need to know the characters in a book, and feel for them. I grew to like Door, and even Richard (who was never as whiny as Arthur Dent but was pretty annoying at times). de Carabas was a treat, and I loved the Tardis-like quality of the Earl's home on the subway carriage, where the outside is defined and confined but the inside is larger than it should be, things like that. I love the concept of creating doors where there aren't any, and the flat-out bizarreness and unpredictablility of London Below.<br /><br />The book itself is a bit predictable at times, but not enough to spoil it. One thing that distracted me was that I couldn't tell if they were above ground at times. It seemed like they were, like the first Floating Market that was held in Harrods, it mentions them walking across the pavement, and the second one is held on an old ship. Only, later, Hunter reveals she can't go to London Above. There were a few others spots too where it wasn't clear if they were above or below.<br /><br />So my main concern with Gaiman - and yes, this is only based on the two books of his that I have read, <em>Stardust</em> being the other - is the mocking way he handles his characters. It makes it hard to really like them, because they're not presented as likeable characters. It also puts a bad taste in my mouth, like Gaiman is scoffing at this story he's written because he's afraid of putting confidence into it in case everyone hates it and leaves him looking silly. I can't really explain the strange, uncomfortable feeling I get reading his books any other way. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15154327847341970447">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1467645455">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1467645455" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson" class="left imgcol" title="Paul Nelson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1434048386p2/7553206.jpg" alt="Paul Nelson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1467645455?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 03, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson" class="user" title="Paul Nelson">Paul Nelson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Paperback 9780060557812" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7553206-paul-nelson?shelf=all-time-favourites" class="actionLinkLite">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7553206-paul-nelson?shelf=2015-books-read" class="actionLinkLite">2015-books-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7553206-paul-nelson?shelf=its-gaiman" class="actionLinkLite">its-gaiman</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1467645455">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6813620279250812846"><em> <strong>"Things to do. People to damage"</strong> </em><br /><br />The audio of Neverwhere narrated by Neil himself was one of my last books of the year but definitely ranks up there as one of my favourites of the year if not all-time.<br /><br />As a narrator Neil Gaiman is something quite special, the different characters are easily distinguishable and I was left hanging on every word by a truly accomplished story-teller and perfect teller of stories.<br /><br />I won't go into the plot detail, the books nearly 20 years old and its all been done a m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6813620279250812846"><em>
  <strong>"Things to do. People to damage"</strong>
</em><br /><br />The audio of Neverwhere narrated by Neil himself was one of my last books of the year but definitely ranks up there as one of my favourites of the year if not all-time.<br /><br />As a narrator Neil Gaiman is something quite special, the different characters are easily distinguishable and I was left hanging on every word by a truly accomplished story-teller and perfect teller of stories.<br /><br />I won't go into the plot detail, the books nearly 20 years old and its all been done a million times before but I am kicking myself for not having read this a hell of a lot sooner.<br /><br />All the characters of London underneath and London overneath in this Neverwhere adventure are distinctly charismatic, magical and captivating. The two characters that for me stole every scene right from their entrance were the terrifyingly funny Mr Croup (the brains and the words) and Mr Vandemar (the blunt brutal one), could it really be anybody else.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong> “There are four simple ways for the observant to tell Mr. Croup and Mr. Vandemar apart: first, Mr. Vandemar is two and a half heads taller than Mr. Croup; second, Mr. Croup has eyes of a faded china blue, while Mr. Vandemar's eyes are brown; third, while Mr. Vandemar fashioned the rings he wears on his right hand out of the skulls of four ravens, Mr. Croup has no obvious jewelery; fourth, Mr. Croup likes words, while Mr. Vandemar is always hungry. Also, they look nothing at all alike.” </strong>
</em> <br /><br />Gaiman makes the city below completely believable to the point where you can picture it in your head, he makes you care for the characters and I was fully invested in the story, the world, everything. The city underneath is that little bit darker, that little bit dirtier matched by the people who live there, there's magical elements, wondrous creatures and a real life Angel, a fantastically grim urban fantasy setting. It's pretty much prefect.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong> “Now me,” said Mr. Vandemar.<br />“What number am I thinking of?” <br />“I beg your pardon?” <br />“What number am I thinking of?” repeated Mr. Vandemar. “It’s between one and a lot,” he added, helpfully.” </strong>
</em> <br /><br />It was cleverly done with Richard, and everyone above forgetting who he was after coming into contact with those from beneath, forcing him to seek Door out and the start of a wonderful adventure. Mr Croup and Mr Vandemar are worthy of more stories, I'd love to read more of them, wickedly entertaining characters, as was the Marquis..<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>'A rustle in the tunnel darkness; Mr. Vandemar's knife was in his hand, and then it was no longer in his hand, and it was quivering gently almost thirty feet away. He walked over to his knife and picked it up by the hilt. There was a gray rat impaled on the blade, its mouth opening and closing impotently as the life fled. He crushed its skull between finger and thumb.'</strong>
</em><br /><br />Apologies I could go quoting crazy here, enough with Croup &amp; Vandermar. And Neverwhere is now a firm favourite.<br /><br />Also posted at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/1317217/neverwhere-by-neil-gaiman" target="_blank">http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6813620279250812846">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_665712802">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/665712802" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4086118-michael" class="left imgcol" title="Michael"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439669517p2/4086118.jpg" alt="Michael" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/665712802?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 01, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4086118-michael" class="user" title="Michael">Michael</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Paperback 9780060557812" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=england" class="actionLinkLite">england</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=london" class="actionLinkLite">london</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer665712802">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer509365144132466148">For me this was just the right balance of whimsy and mythological drama. A fun urban fantasy refreshingly free of vampires and werewolves. There is real elegance how it hooks you in and takes you on a wild ride. The heroes are minimally sketched ciphers the readers are invited to project themselves into. They take shape mainly from their quests: Richard wants to get back his ordinary boring life; Door wants to avenge the murder of her family; Hunter wants to kill the Great Beast of London. They</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText509365144132466148">For me this was just the right balance of whimsy and mythological drama. A fun urban fantasy refreshingly free of vampires and werewolves. There is real elegance how it hooks you in and takes you on a wild ride. The heroes are minimally sketched ciphers the readers are invited to project themselves into. They take shape mainly from their quests: Richard wants to get back his ordinary boring life; Door wants to avenge the murder of her family; Hunter wants to kill the Great Beast of London. They join forces to overcome several challenges in the weird and scary underground world of the “London Below”. The power structure of this society depends on bartering and favors, so it is impossible to tell who to trust. The most evil and supernaturally powerful characters in this tale, Mr. Vandemar and Mr. Croup, take so much fun in their mayhem, you can’t help liking them (“Can't make an omelette without killing a few people”). If you want to know if the book is the right read for you, the time it takes to peruse a reasonable sample of the 7,000 reviews on Goodreads might better be spent just diving into the rabbit hole and reading the book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="509365144132466148">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer831623789">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6719241474438402973"><br /><strong> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/4729956-crystal-craig?shelf=recommended">Recommended Reading</a> </strong><br /><br /><strong> <em>"Dear Diary, he began. On Friday, I had a job, a fiancée, a home, and a life that made sense. (Well, as much as any life makes sense). Then I found an injured girl bleeding on the pavement, and I tried to be a Good Samaritan. Now I've got no fiancée, no home, no job, and I'm walking around a couple of hundred feet under the streets of London with the projected life expectancy of a suicidal fruitfly."</em> </strong><br /><br />Neil Gaiman read the audio version of his novel, Neverwhere. He did an exc</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6719241474438402973"><br /><strong>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/4729956-crystal-craig?shelf=recommended">Recommended Reading</a>
</strong><br /><br /><strong>
  <em>"Dear Diary, he began. On Friday, I had a job, a fiancée, a home, and a life that made sense. (Well, as much as any life makes sense). Then I found an injured girl bleeding on the pavement, and I tried to be a Good Samaritan. Now I've got no fiancée, no home, no job, and I'm walking around a couple of hundred feet under the streets of London with the projected life expectancy of a suicidal fruitfly."</em>
</strong><br /><br />Neil Gaiman read the audio version of his novel, Neverwhere. He did an excellent job portraying the insecure voice of the main character, Richard Mayhew. I didn't enjoy Neverwhere as much as I did The Ocean at the End of the Lane, but still it was a fun read. Neverwhere was my second Neil Gaiman book, and I can understand why so many readers enjoy his work. He has quite the imagination. His books are like a Tim Burton movie. I loved London Below and all the characters; Richard, Door, the Marquis, Hunter, and most of all: villains Croup and Vandemar. <br /><br />Awesome book. Very well-written. A solid four stars. I look forward to discovering more of Mr. Gaiman's work. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_716902827">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716902827" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell" class="left imgcol" title="Ronyell"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1423803024p2/1169488.jpg" alt="Ronyell" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/716902827?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 04, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell" class="user" title="Ronyell">Ronyell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Paperback 9780060557812" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=neil-gaiman" class="actionLinkLite">neil-gaiman</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=sexy-good-girl-heroine" class="actionLinkLite">sexy-good-girl-heroine</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=urban-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=adult-book" class="actionLinkLite">adult-book</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=read-in-2013" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=setting-in-britain" class="actionLinkLite">setting-in-britain</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-heroine" class="actionLinkLite">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-hero" class="actionLinkLite">strong-hero</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews" class="actionLinkLite">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=ronyell-s-epinions-reviews" class="actionLinkLite">ronyell-s-epinions-reviews</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer716902827">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1927535287230251781"><img width="400" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="Neverwhere" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382334831i/5827530.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong> <em>“Imagine living in a world where you think that everything has become familiar to you, but then you realize that there is a different world far beyond the one you know.”</em> </strong><br /><br />I have not read much of Neil Gaiman’s books geared towards adults, until I first read “American Gods,” which was a book that I enjoyed intensely. But now, I have a new favorite from Neil Gaiman’s books geared towards adults and that is “Neverwhere!” Full of adventure, horror and romance, “Neverwhere” is certainly one of Neil Ga</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1927535287230251781"><img width="400" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="Neverwhere" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382334831i/5827530.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“Imagine living in a world where you think that everything has become familiar to you, but then you realize that there is a different world far beyond the one you know.”</em>
</strong><br /><br />I have not read much of Neil Gaiman’s books geared towards adults, until I first read “American Gods,” which was a book that I enjoyed intensely. But now, I have a new favorite from Neil Gaiman’s books geared towards adults and that is “Neverwhere!” Full of adventure, horror and romance, “Neverwhere” is certainly one of Neil Gaiman’s greatest works yet!<br /><br />Richard Mayhew was an average young man who lived a normal life and had a fiancée named Jessica. One night however, Richard meets up with a young girl named Door who he found bleeding on the London sidewalk and he immediately goes and try to tend to her wounds. But, once Richard performs this heroic act, he will soon discover that his life will change forever when he seems to have vanished from the face of the earth and ends up in an alternative world of London, London Below. Now, Richard must help Door from being killed by the murderous Mr. Croup and Mr. Vandemar or London Below will be in great danger!<br /><br />Wow! This book was simply amazing! What made this book such a joy to read was the fact that Richard ends up in an alternative universe of London and he realizes that London Below is far more dangerous and different than the London he knew from above! I loved the way that Neil Gaiman made this story so intense and even scary at times, especially whenever the scenes involving Mr. Croup and Mr. Vandemar showed up in the story. I was seriously scared of Mr. Croup and Mr. Vandemar as they were hired by a mysterious person to kill Door at all costs and they are certainly professionals in that field! But, what was the most chilling aspect of Mr. Croup and Mr. Vandemar’s characters was that they would just calmly tell their victims about how they will torture them and their torturing methods were truly graphic and disturbing to say the least! I really loved the characters featured in this book, especially Richard Mayhew and Door as they were truly interesting characters and they brought so much depth and intensity to the story. I did find it heartbreaking that Richard could not get back to his real home in London and all the other characters telling him that it would be impossible to get back to London Above definitely made me feel even worse for Richard. At the same time, I loved the fact that Richard was such a caring and curious person as I completely sympathize with his confusion in understanding the strange cultures of London Below. I loved the way that Neil Gaiman went into so much detail about the different cultures of London Below from London Above and I also loved the fact that Neil Gaiman included some historical notes about London’s history and weaved them into the story with such clarity. Door was another character that I really enjoyed as she was such a strange yet interesting character. I loved the fact that Door just plunges into a situation because of her knowledge of London Below as it proves that she is a truly brave character! I really loved the Marquis de Carabas, even though at first, he annoyed me a bit at the beginning. But, once the story starts progressing, I found myself loving the Marquis de Carabas more and more as he proves to be quite a surprising character. I loved the eerie atmosphere of this story as I was literally sitting on the edge of my seat, wondering if Richard, Door, Hunter and the Marquis de Carabas will ever find their destination and try to survive London Below without being killed by Mr. Croup and Mr. Vandemar. What really stood out for me in this story was the fact that it was like a darker version of “Alice in Wonderland” and I really liked that dark and gritty aspect to this story.<br /><br /><img width="400" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="Neverwhere" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382334831i/5827531.jpg" /><br /><br />The only problems with this book are that it has some strong language, although it does not occur frequently and some scary situations involving the characters being placed in great peril. Some readers might find some parts of this book a bit too dark and creepy, such as the scenes involving Mr. Croup and Mr. Vandemar.<br /><br />Overall, “Neverwhere” is a truly brilliant book that deals with deciding what you really want out of life and is probably one of the best books that use dark fantasy in its finest! I would strongly recommend this book to any fan of Neil Gaiman’s works!<br /><br /><img width="300" height="200" class="escapedImg" alt="Banner" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385664778i/7198025._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>Review is also on: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2013/10/neverwhere-by-neil-gaiman.html">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1927535287230251781">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer29821348">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13055040454783574947">6.0 stars. One of my ALL Time Favorite novels. Neil Gaiman's ability to create "original" characters and settings that virtually leap off the page at you is astounding. This ia a true gem of a book and is highly recommended for anyone who enjoys great writing with superb characters. HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION!!!<br /><br />Nominee: British Fantasy Award<br />Nominee: Mythopoeic Fantasy Award </span>

      <a href="/user/show/5253785-lyn" class="user" title="Lyn">Lyn</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Paperback 9780060557812" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer350099233">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16607232346025254611">Upon beginning a review of Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman my first thoughts were to write that even a bad Gaiman novel was better than most other authors best work. <br /><br />But this is unfair, Neverwhere is not a “bad” novel at all. <br /><br />Compared to <a title="Stardust by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16793.Stardust">Stardust</a> or <a title="Anansi Boys (American Gods, #2) by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2744.Anansi_Boys__American_Gods___2_">Anansi Boys</a>, or especially the masterpiece <a title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_">American Gods</a>, it lacks the epic presence and may even be categorized as one of Gaiman’s lesser works. <br /><br />What is present, though, is Gaiman’s phenomenal writing, his brilliant and original imagination and his abilit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16607232346025254611">Upon beginning a review of Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman my first thoughts were to write that even a bad Gaiman novel was better than most other authors best work. <br /><br />But this is unfair, Neverwhere is not a “bad” novel at all. <br /><br />Compared to <a title="Stardust by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16793.Stardust">Stardust</a> or <a title="Anansi Boys (American Gods, #2) by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2744.Anansi_Boys__American_Gods___2_">Anansi Boys</a>, or especially the masterpiece <a title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_">American Gods</a>, it lacks the epic presence and may even be categorized as one of Gaiman’s lesser works. <br /><br />What is present, though, is Gaiman’s phenomenal writing, his brilliant and original imagination and his ability to simply tell a good story. This was entertaining and the literary ground is ripe for more Neverwhere adventures if he ever decided to return, and he has hinted that he may. <br /><br /><img width="400" height="400" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435879256i/15383954._SY540_.jpg" /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_17497789">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17497789" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/520753-kim" class="left imgcol" title="Kim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1402541317p2/520753.jpg" alt="Kim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/17497789?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 03, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/520753-kim" class="user" title="Kim">Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Paperback 9780060557812" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=gr-friend-recommendations" class="actionLinkLite">gr-friend-recommendations</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=mmxi" class="actionLinkLite">mmxi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer17497789">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9897617312711818044">My only experience with Neil Gaiman’s writing (other than a viewing of Coraline) was Anansi Boys, which happened to be the sequel to American Gods to which no one had bothered to tell me about. So, yeah, I was hesitant. I mean really… of all the people on this site that I know that like Gaiman, couldn’t one of you have bothered to let me know? Huh? Fine. It’s done with.<br /><br />Now, erasing that slight… really, I am… I will tell you that I totally gave Gaiman the brush off. I filed him under ‘what the he</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9897617312711818044">My only experience with Neil Gaiman’s writing (other than a viewing of Coraline) was Anansi Boys, which happened to be the sequel to American Gods to which no one had bothered to tell me about. So, yeah, I was hesitant. I mean really… of all the people on this site that I know that like Gaiman, couldn’t one of you have bothered to let me know? Huh? Fine. It’s done with.<br /><br />Now, erasing that slight… really, I am… I will tell you that I totally gave Gaiman the brush off. I filed him under ‘what the hell’, ‘hype’, ‘don’t give a damn’ and ‘world weary.’ <br /><br />My bad. <br /><br />Neverwhere is brimming with exotic personalities who have ‘fallen between the cracks’ and landed in ‘London Below’, the place below the sewers and train tunnels, where rats have kingdoms and Night is still an idea that is terrifying. The plot is a familiar one, there is a quest, there are bad guys, there is the hesitant hero and a rakish Marquis. Oh, and there’s Door, the determined princess in distress. But Gaiman’s writing creeps along the sewers and delivers us to angels in a way that takes your breath away. <br /><br /><em>“And then it erupted over the side of the platform. It was diaphanous, dreamlike, a ghost-thing, the color of black smoke, and it welled up like silk under water, and, moving astonishingly fast while still seeming to drift almost in slow motion, it wrapped itself tightly around Richard’s ankle.” </em><br /><br />I wonder sometimes what falling through the cracks would be like. If everyone that I knew suddenly ‘unknew’ me. Would I go mad? Would I huddle in doorways and wait for the gloaming to swallow me? Could I survive? (Seriously, help me out here...I'm all for huddling...)Our hero, Richard, meets Hunters and Velvets and Earls and assassins that make those creepy floaty <a rel="nofollow" href="http://buffyd6.tripod.com/images/17hush.jpg">dudes</a> from Buffy episode Season 4, #10 look like Hummels. Richard, of course, is made better by knowing these creatures and learns that life isn’t all about corner offices and pretentious fiancés..and that sometimes angels can be assholes, but we already knew that, right? <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9897617312711818044">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_23625941">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23625941" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-fabulous-fabulaphile" class="left imgcol" title="colleen the fabulous fabulaphile"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1449972869p2/1209800.jpg" alt="colleen the fabulous fabulaphile" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/23625941?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 07, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-fabulous-fabulaphile" class="user" title="colleen the fabulous fabulaphile">colleen the fabulous fabulaphile</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/474072.Neverwhere" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380789016" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes a good story </span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-fabulous-fabulaphile?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-fabulous-fabulaphile?shelf=urban-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-fabulous-fabulaphile?shelf=dark-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-fabulous-fabulaphile?shelf=loved" class="actionLinkLite">loved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer23625941">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14877570175437887898">After reading <em>Neverwhere</em> for the second time, it remains one of, if not thee, favorite book of mine by Gaiman. There really aren't many flaws to this book. I love the world and the idea that the people who 'slip through the cracks' exist in this other world beneath the world. I even love the slight ambiguity that it could be that Richard is actually just crazy, through I prefer to think of it as real.<br /><br />I love the way the story unfolds. We are given information piece-meal, receiving it as our prota</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14877570175437887898">After reading <em>Neverwhere</em> for the second time, it remains one of, if not thee, favorite book of mine by Gaiman. There really aren't many flaws to this book. I love the world and the idea that the people who 'slip through the cracks' exist in this other world beneath the world. I even love the slight ambiguity that it could be that Richard is actually just crazy, through I prefer to think of it as real.<br /><br />I love the way the story unfolds. We are given information piece-meal, receiving it as our protagonist receives it, and, like our protagonist, we just sort of go along for the ride and start taking the craziness for granted, because it's told in such a convincing way that you don't really ever stop to think it couldn't be true.<br /><br />I love the characters. Richard is a bit dull and gets annoying sometimes. Door is interesting though, in a way, oddly underdeveloped. The Marquis de Carabas is one of my faves, though, and who doesn't love the creepy, funny insanity of Croup and Vandemar?<br /><br />I love the wording. Gaiman is evocative without being overly desriptive or trite. The story moves along at a good pace, and the words wrap around you, creating the world and the story, with turns of phrases that just linger on the tongue and in the mind.<br /><br />*some spoilers*<br /><br />And, lastly, I love the ending. There are many self-referential nods to Wizard of Oz throughout the story. It's obvious - the journey to the angel to get knowledge, or power, or to go home. Even Croup and Vandemar as a substitute Witch, as they hound the heroes with threats throughout the story. But in this Oz, which I still choose to think of as more than a dream, the theme is that getting what you want, what you think you wanted all along, isn't necessarily the best thing for you. I always thought Dorothy was better off in Oz, just like Richard truly belongs in London Below.<br /><br />There are few perfect endings to books, but I think this is one... I always sigh happily to myself when it's over... <br /><br />Ok - I lied, that's not the last thing I'm going to say. I also really like how Richard, our bumbling hero, isn't always the hero. Yes, he passes some ordeals - but he still has to be saved from his encounter with heights. And he doesn't really rescue to damsel, even though it seems that's how it's going to turn out. Rather the damsel rescues them all, through cleverness.<br /><br />And I also like how it doesn't become a romance between Richard and Door. I don't have anything against romances, as evidence by my reading list, but it's nice that it doesn't have to be that way. <br /><br />*end spoilers*<br /><br />Overall, there's not really much to dislike about this book - unless you're just a big curmudgeon or something ;)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14877570175437887898">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_206622417">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206622417" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite" class="left imgcol" title="Erin (Paperbackstash) *Book Hoarders Unite!*"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448768136p2/3048260.jpg" alt="Erin (Paperbackstash) *Book Hoarders Unite!*" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/206622417?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite" class="user" title="Erin (Paperbackstash) *Book Hoarders Unite!*">Erin (Paperbackstash) *Book Hoarders Unite!*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/474072.Neverwhere" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380789016" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=a-own-book-form" class="actionLinkLite">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=urban-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=magic-powers" class="actionLinkLite">magic-powers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=4-star" class="actionLinkLite">4-star</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer206622417">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer35852845123710814"><br /><strong>“I mean, maybe I am crazy. I mean, maybe. But if this is all there is, then I don't want to be sane.” </strong><br /><br />Neverwhere – what genre to call it? Difficult to define – the popular shelf label is Urban Fantasy, but to me it’s not quite that since it takes place mainly in a fantasy setting. Horror is certainly present, especially from the diabolical hands of the twisted villains, complete with gory tidbits. Ultimately I’m settling on Dark Fantasy since it’s more of an adult fairytale with horror twists.<br /><br />Th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText35852845123710814"><br /><strong>“I mean, maybe I am crazy. I mean, maybe. But if this is all there is, then I don't want to be sane.” </strong><br /><br />Neverwhere – what genre to call it? Difficult to define – the popular shelf label is Urban Fantasy, but to me it’s not quite that since it takes place mainly in a fantasy setting. Horror is certainly present, especially from the diabolical hands of the twisted villains, complete with gory tidbits. Ultimately I’m settling on Dark Fantasy since it’s more of an adult fairytale with horror twists.<br /><br />This was my first read of Gaiman, and I have to say I’m impressed – he has a colorful way of weaving scenes where they’re burned firmly in your psyche without having to dig into the bag of excessive descriptions and tedious derailing. Some of the sentences are downright poetic, but the bulk of the writing is straightforward polish.<br /><br />Characters are another successful feat. Richard, a good person overruled in his personal life by those more aggressive, works well as the lead when he’s absorbed into this distasteful world. The Marquis was varied with his scope of being both likeable and unlikeable; his scenes proved he was one of the better characters with his dry humor and never knowing quite where you stood with him. Not knowing whether he could be trusted, not sure which side he was on till the end, made him stand out as a delight to read about.<br /><br />Croup and Vandemar are some of the more unique villains I’ve had the pleasure of reading. They’re insane but almost amusing with their bizarre dialogues, viewpoints, and personality oddities – clever with their killing and torture ability, top notch at finding their prey, and able to create chills for the reader when they’re zooming in on their victims. I never saw some of the surprises with who they ended up working with.<br /><br />While rich in fairy tale fantasy, it’s not confusing if you keep reading, the world being a complex build of chilling monstrosities (especially that bridge of darkness), creative otherworldly beings (rat speakers and the twists of raising the rats to a higher level in London of all places...), and fantastical elements including angels, secret doors, and created portals.<br /><br />Pacing comes in an even hand, there’s heavily applied suspense during nail-biting scenes, and there are plenty of surprises to wrap scenes with. The ending choice on Richard’s size wasn’t a surprise, but even with the boring life he’s returning to, I doubt I’d have chosen the same fate as he did.<br /><br />Definitely worth a read – will be checking out more of the author’s work in the near future.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="35852845123710814">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_672382786">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/672382786" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/695116-jim" class="left imgcol" title="Jim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" alt="Jim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/672382786?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/695116-jim" class="user" title="Jim">Jim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/105732.Neverwhere" title="Audio CD 9780061373879" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction" class="actionLinkLite">2fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1audio" class="actionLinkLite">1audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer672382786">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13341218610366534381">The story was unique, ingenious, &amp; interesting. The magic is capricious, the characters memorable, &amp; the plot had me biting my nails as it twisted about. The overall theme of the invisible people was haunting. There was a lot of understated British humor and it was very well read by its author.<br /><br />I wanted to kick the main character pretty much all the way through the book, although the rest of the characters were great. I especially liked the pair of assassins. They were so perfectly evil y</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13341218610366534381">The story was unique, ingenious, &amp; interesting. The magic is capricious, the characters memorable, &amp; the plot had me biting my nails as it twisted about. The overall theme of the invisible people was haunting. There was a lot of understated British humor and it was very well read by its author.<br /><br />I wanted to kick the main character pretty much all the way through the book, although the rest of the characters were great. I especially liked the pair of assassins. They were so perfectly evil yet had a wonderfully comic facade.<br /><br />I didn't give this 5 stars for a couple of reasons. I'm not much of a fan of British humor, so while it was amusing once, I'll never want to read this again. There were a few logical issues in the story, too. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Door &amp; the Beast of London statuette - she let the Marquis take it, didn't seem to think it important, yet knew about it when going through the maze. The way Hunter &amp; Door left Richard with the lamia &amp; never warned him about her. The lamia's character &amp; purpose seemed tacked on to add to the word count. Richard killing the beast so easily even with Hunter egging it on. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> None were huge, but they seemed to pile up at the end. <br /><br />The last chapter was redundant. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Richard was a complete nonentity in the real world - that was the whole point. Only someone naturally on the brink could have seen Door &amp; would have so completely &amp; easily disappeared with so little contact. He finally became someone &amp; made true friends in the underside, so a paragraph or two of reflection would have served to make the point. That it took an entire chapter to bring him around made me want to kick him again, just when I was finally beginning to like him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I was very pleased by Gaiman's reading. The British pronounce some things rather oddly (I'm an American. The way I pronounce words is correct. I don't care if they do lay first claim to the language. ;-)  ), but that added to the feel of the story. He certainly put a lot of emotion into it &amp; that did cause some problems trying to listen while using machinery. His voice would soften too much with some characters in some situations while others were very loud.<br /><br />Overall, I'd give this a 3.5. I won't rush right out to find another novel by him, though. I've read one as a graphic novel &amp; it was pretty good. This as an audio was far better.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13341218610366534381">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_237651515">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237651515" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6390827-tamsien-west" class="left imgcol" title="Tamsien West"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1321595115p2/6390827.jpg" alt="Tamsien West" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/237651515?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 10, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6390827-tamsien-west" class="user" title="Tamsien West">Tamsien West</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/23462649-neverwhere" title="Hardcover 9780062371058" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6390827-tamsien-west?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6390827-tamsien-west?shelf=urban-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6390827-tamsien-west?shelf=favourite-books" class="actionLinkLite">favourite-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6390827-tamsien-west?shelf=read-along" class="actionLinkLite">read-along</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer237651515">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9413079250939143889">I had tears in my eyes as I read the last few pages of Neverwhere, and I can’t fully express how much I adore this story. In rereading it I remembered all the reasons I loved this book when I first read it almost 10 years ago, and all the reasons Neil Gaiman became and remains one of my favourite authors. I felt like I was coming home to visit an old friend, and in conversation with them realising our relationship goes so much deeper than superficial pleasantries about comings and goings, and in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9413079250939143889">I had tears in my eyes as I read the last few pages of Neverwhere, and I can’t fully express how much I adore this story. In rereading it I remembered all the reasons I loved this book when I first read it almost 10 years ago, and all the reasons Neil Gaiman became and remains one of my favourite authors. I felt like I was coming home to visit an old friend, and in conversation with them realising our relationship goes so much deeper than superficial pleasantries about comings and goings, and in fact it is founded on something rich and wonderful. As a 17 year old I loved the creative world Gaiman created, the colourful characters and vivid settings of London Below, I loved the sly humour and all of the puns. As a 26 year old I connected with Richard’s struggle between the pull of a ‘simple’ life that meets expectations, and the path less travelled that my heart tugs me towards.<br /><br />Neverwhere is ostensibly a story about an Englishman, Richard, who is ordinary in every way. Living an ordinary life in London, with ordinary friends, and a girlfriend who kind of wishes he was a bit more ordinary. His life changes when he ‘falls through the cracks’ and into the mysterious London Below, and is swept away on an adventure with an assortment of unusual characters. It sounds relatively straightforward as fantasy tales go, but it is so much more than these bare bones. Gaiman’s wit and tenderness transform it into a deeply compelling and amusing story that draws on lots of traditional fairy tales (Alice in Wonderland is referenced directly more than once, as is Puss in Boots).<br /><br />On a different note I am fascinated by Gaiman’s inclusion of diverse characters throughout Neverwhere. The Marquis &amp; Hunter are people of colour, though their backgrounds not really explored, as are the Black Friars. Meanwhile Hunter’s sexuality is clear but not a topic of any particular focus. Did anyone else notice this throughout the novel? In a great blog post Laura Zats says “…literature is both imaginative and representative. It reflects who we are, and who we want to be”. She neatly sums up my thoughts on Gaiman’s ability to ensure that “race is just one facet of a person’s identity, just as it is in reality. He acknowledges it, but doesn’t let it become all a character is.” and I would extend this to sexual orientation as well.<br /><br />For those of you who have not read many of Gaiman’s books this might seem like drawing a long conclusion from something which is not a huge deal in the book. But when you look at his body of work as a whole, Neverwhere being just the very first novel he published, and see these themes and approaches are running throughout regardless of genre or subject matter, to me that is the mark of a writer who truly understands just how important literature is in shaping how we see ourselves and how we understand the world. And it makes me glad that he writes, and is so widely read.<br /><br />Neverwhere is one of those books that I love so much I will continue to recommend it to everyone who shows even a passing interest in reading a word printed on a page. However I should acknowledge that it is probably not for everyone. It has a very particular ‘British-ness’ about it, and the humour is very dry, it is a story of self discovery, not of glory, and there is no real romance to speak of. The world is not ‘well developed’ in the way YA fantasy readers of the recent trends in trilogies would expect, and you will definitely end the book with more questions than answers. But all of those things are things that I love about Neverwhere, and about Gaiman’s writing, and they are the reasons that Neverwhere will remain forever and always one of my favourite books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9413079250939143889">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_824635578">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/824635578" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/27528763-gary" class="left imgcol" title="Gary "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1433945411p2/27528763.jpg" alt="Gary " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/824635578?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 22, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/27528763-gary" class="user" title="Gary ">Gary </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Paperback 9780060557812" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/27528763-gary?shelf=dark-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer824635578">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4279896717469259187">When I first started this book, I had to force myself to keep going. Having read American Gods by Gaiman, I was expecting a similar read. While similar, it did not grab my attention in the same way and I left this book only to come back to try again. I was glad I did.<br />In the beginning, it feels like Gaiman is trying too hard to establish himself as a writer of "weird" or mythological tales. Everything has a disjointed, hallucinogenic, surreal quality that was not pulling me into the storyline. <br />At</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4279896717469259187">When I first started this book, I had to force myself to keep going. Having read American Gods by Gaiman, I was expecting a similar read. While similar, it did not grab my attention in the same way and I left this book only to come back to try again. I was glad I did.<br />In the beginning, it feels like Gaiman is trying too hard to establish himself as a writer of "weird" or mythological tales. Everything has a disjointed, hallucinogenic, surreal quality that was not pulling me into the storyline. <br />At some point, however, Gaiman quit trying to create a style for himself and began simply writing in the style that clearly is his own. He begins to focus on the characters and the development of the storyline rather than atmospherics and weirdness (although it does stay weird). It almost feels like you can see him mature as a writer and find himself in the world of novels.<br />Although the plot does take a "run and fetch this and that" quest in an Alice in Wonderland type of world, the characters become likable at some point. Soon I found myself wondering what would happen to them, and perhaps more importantly, caring. I had planned on rating this three stars (with a footnote indicating 3.5), but I found the conclusion so satisfying I give it four stars and will return to another of Gaiman's works in the future. Soon.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4279896717469259187">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BVc5fwmKmfzq4zTGVecPNlAt5PlT+ADi/KEVy5Ndk8tggwas+1iNBmY7QH0rhumEGdon4BolR0iWqBBZX8hljg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

On Armada, everyone is given work, and even Remades live as equals to humans, Cactae, and Cray. Yet no one may ever leave.Lonely and embittered in her captivity, Bellis knows that to show dissent is a death sentence. Instead, she must furtively seek information about Armada’s agenda.
